**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is June, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

**Step 1 (logic-heavy)**

Define the Categories: 

Read through the titles of hundreds of news articles and think carefully.  Use your memory fully. Define major areas, and define specific topics under each area, in a hierarchical way. Every news article should have its best-fitting category. There should be two hierarchical tiers (area, topic), instead of three, and then we get down to individual articles. You should consider this very carefully, making the categories the most helpful for human cognition. Control the total number of areas to 5-8, depending on how diverse and complex the topics are. Remember to group similar categories together closely. Do not let similar categories stay far from each other.  Compile all your in a simple text file (step1.txt).

**Summary of Revisions:**

After reviewing the initial categories against the full list of headlines, I have made the following adjustments to create a more logical and useful framework:

1.  **Renamed and Refined Areas:**
    *   Area 1 was renamed to "US-Iran Escalation and Ceasefire" to better reflect the full narrative arc present in the headlines, from initial strikes to the reported resolution.
    *   The original "Social and Cultural Issues" area has been broadened to "Public Policy and Social Issues" to logically include health and environmental news that didn't fit well elsewhere.
    *   "Foreign Relations and National Security (Non-Iran)" was shortened to "Foreign Relations and National Security" for conciseness, as the context makes its non-Iran focus clear.
    *   "Domestic Governance and Inter-Branch Politics" was simplified to "Domestic Governance and Politics."

2.  **Reorganized Topics for Thematic Cohesion:**
    *   **Judicial Rulings:** Instead of grouping all judicial actions into one area, I've placed them within their relevant policy domains to provide better context. Supreme Court rulings on deportation are now directly under "Immigration and Border Security," which is more useful for understanding that specific issue. Other legal/judicial stories (e.g., DOJ lawsuits, non-immigration SCOTUS decisions) are now consolidated under "Legal and Judicial Developments" within the broader "Domestic Governance" area.
    *   **Health and Environment:** Topics like health plan reforms, CDC appointments, and state-level environmental regulations have been grouped together under the new "Public Policy and Social Issues" area, providing a clear home for these important but less frequent topics.
    *   **State-Level News:** Multiple stories about policy decisions and political conflicts in Texas and Florida are now consolidated under Topic 3.3, "State-Level Policy and Political Conflicts," highlighting the trend of significant state-level political action.

These changes result in a six-area structure that is balanced, comprehensive, and aligns the news thematically, which should be more intuitive and actionable for the congressional leadership receiving the briefing.

**Scoring Criteria:**

*   **Articles (1-10):** Scores are based on source reliability (e.g., Reuters, AP, FT are high-tier; partisan or niche blogs are low-tier) and the significance of the event described in the headline (e.g., a ceasefire announcement is more important than a minor political feud).

*   **Areas (1-10):** Scores reflect the overall weight and urgency of the topics contained within them, providing a high-level view of the day's most critical news themes.

This system is designed to objectively rank the news flow, prioritizing actionable intelligence for leadership.

**Area 1: US-Iran Escalation and Ceasefire**

**Topic 1.1: Ceasefire Announcement and De-escalation**

The immediate crisis with Iran appears to have culminated in a ceasefire. President Trump announced an agreement between Iran and Israel, a development reported by multiple major news outlets [1, 2]. This announcement capped a period of rapid de-escalation that began with the President's public framing of Iran's preceding military actions. Following Iran's attack on a U.S. base, President Trump characterized the retaliatory strike as "very weak," noting that Tehran had provided "'early notice'" [3]. In a highly publicized statement, he also explicitly thanked Iran for its “‘very weak’ response” to U.S. airstrikes, a move that appears to have significantly altered the trajectory of the conflict [4].

**DAILY BRIEFING FOR CONGRESSIONAL LEADERSHIP**
**June 2025 – CHIEF NEWS ANALYST**

**Area 1: US-Iran Escalation and Ceasefire**

**Topic 1.1: Ceasefire Announcement and De-escalation**

The immediate crisis with Iran appears to have culminated in a ceasefire. President Trump announced an agreement between Iran and Israel, a development confirmed by major news outlets [1]. This announcement capped a period of rapid de-escalation that began with the President's public framing of Iran's preceding military actions. Following Iran's attack on a U.S. base, President Trump characterized the retaliatory strike as "very weak," noting that Tehran had provided "'early notice'" [2]. In a highly publicized statement, he also explicitly thanked Iran for its “‘very weak’ response” to U.S. airstrikes, a move that appears to have significantly altered the trajectory of the conflict [3].

[1] Trump announces Israel-Iran ceasefire, https://www.politico.com/news/2025/06/23/israel-iran-ceasefire-trump-00419364

[2] Trump calls Iran's retaliatory strike ‘very weak,' says country gave 'early notice' of attack, https://www.pbs.org/newshour/politics/trump-calls-irans-retaliatory-strike-very-weak-says-country-gave-early-notice-of-attack

[3] Donald Trump thanks Iran for ‘very weak’ response to US air strikes, https://www.ft.com/content/67207725-da79-4c3b-9ced-0479adb0da06

**Topic 1.2: Iranian Retaliation and Regional Escalation**

Prior to the de-escalation, Iran launched retaliatory missile attacks directly targeting a U.S. military base in Qatar [1, 2]. The direct military confrontation sharply increased regional volatility, prompting Gulf neighbors to close their airspace to civilian and commercial traffic [3]. The action was not entirely unexpected; the FBI had previously issued a public warning that retaliation from Iran was a distinct possibility following the initial U.S. strikes on Iranian nuclear facilities [4].

[1] Iran launches missiles at US military base in Qatar in retaliation for American bombing, https://apnews.com/article/israel-iran-war-nuclear-trump-bomber-news-06-23-2025-9e78510c88ccc5e262341f41550609c5

**Topic 1.3: US Airstrikes: Justification, Legality, and Execution**

The intelligence basis and legality of the U.S. airstrikes that precipitated the crisis remain subjects of intense debate. Citing U.S. intelligence, Senator Markwayne Mullin stated that Iran had not moved nuclear material from its Fordo facility before the attack [1]. However, Vice President JD Vance subsequently hinted that uranium might have been moved after President Trump’s public statements potentially tipped off Tehran [2]. This has fueled internal concerns, with one report alleging that some military officials viewed the President as the "'biggest threat' to operational security" and planned the operation around him [3]. Others question if the attack "completely missed its mark," contributing to the escalation [4]. The legality of the strikes is also facing challenges from legal analysts, who claim they violate both international law and the U.S. Constitution [5]. Concurrent with these events, the President has publicly floated the idea of pursuing regime change in Iran [6].

**Topic 1.4: International Reaction and Diplomatic Fallout**

The U.S. military action against Iran triggered sharp condemnation from key international leaders. Russian President Vladimir Putin warned the strikes are pushing the world toward a "'very dangerous line'" [1], while French President Emmanuel Macron stated bluntly that the strikes "aren’t legal" under international law [2]. The administration has pushed back on Russian criticism, with President Trump publicly slamming Russia's Medvedev for suggesting other nations might provide Iran with nuclear warheads in response [3].

[1] Putin Says US Strikes on Iran Are Pushing World to 'Very Dangerous Line', https://www.usnews.com/news/world/articles/2025-06-23/irans-supreme-leader-asks-putin-to-do-more-after-us-strikes

**Topic 1.5: Domestic Political Reaction and Congressional Debate**

The strikes have exposed deep divisions within both parties and across the government. Speaker Mike Johnson has come out in opposition to a bipartisan war powers resolution that would retroactively authorize the military action [1]. The Democratic caucus also appears fractured, with one report claiming "Democrats Can’t Get On the Same Page," a sentiment echoed by Senator John Fetterman, who stated his party "has been often wrong" on Iran [2]. On the Republican side, a notable fissure has opened, with staunch presidential ally Rep. Marjorie Taylor Greene calling the administration's actions a "'complete bait and switch'" [3]. This political turmoil unfolds as a recent Reuters/Ipsos poll indicates a majority of Americans are worried the conflict could escalate further [4].

**Topic 2.1: Supreme Court Rulings Bolster Deportation Authority**

The Supreme Court has handed the Trump administration two major victories, significantly expanding executive power over deportations. In a landmark ruling, the Court lifted prior limits, allowing the administration to "swiftly deport certain immigrants" to "third countries" that are not their countries of origin [1, 2]. In a separate but related case, the Court sided with the administration by blocking a lower court's rule regarding deportation notices, further strengthening the executive branch's hand in removal proceedings [3].
